<DL compact>
<DT><FONT SIZE=2>(1)</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Income
from operations and EBITDA are presented before consideration of any management fees paid to us, before the Lawrenceburg 42.5% minority interest and before the Sioux City 30%
minority interest for the period prior to our July&nbsp;2000 acquisition of this minority interest.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT><FONT SIZE=2>(2)</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Excludes
a $6.8&nbsp;million pretax charge related to the write-off of assets for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT><FONT SIZE=2>(3)</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>"EBITDA"
is defined as earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation and amortization and is presented before any management fees paid to Argosy. EBITDA should not be construed as
an alternative to operating income, or net income (as determined in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles) as an indicator of our operating performance, or as an alternative to cash
flows generated by operating, investing and financing activities (as an indicator of cash flow or a measure of liquidity). EBITDA is presented solely as a supplemental disclosure because management
believes that it is a widely used measure of operating performance in the gaming industry and for companies with a significant amount of depreciation and amortization. EBITDA may not be comparable to
similarly titled measures reported by other companies. We have other significant uses of cash flows, including debt service and capital expenditures, which are not reflected in EBITDA.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT><FONT SIZE=2>(4)</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>The
Lawrenceburg partnership pays a financial advisory fee equal to 5.0% of its EBITDA to a minority partner.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT><FONT SIZE=2>(5)</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Jazz
Enterprises,&nbsp;Inc. is a wholly-owned subsidiary that owns and operates the Catfish Town real estate development adjacent to the Company's Baton Rouge casino. </FONT></DD></DL>
<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>21</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=4,SEQ=22,EFW="2037759",CP="ARGOSY GAMING COMPANY",DN="1",CHK=181939,FOLIO='21',FILE='DISK011:[01CHI9.01CHI1459]DK1459A.;31',USER='MWEINST',CD='15-FEB-2001;11:28' -->
<A NAME="page_dk1459_1_22"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="dk1459_year_ended_december_31,_2000_c__yea01868"> </A>
<A NAME="toc_dk1459_8"> </A></FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><B>Year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000 compared to year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999    <BR>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Casino</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Casino revenues for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000, increased $99.7&nbsp;million,
or 17.8%, to $658.9&nbsp;million from $559.1&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999. The western properties (Alton, Riverside, Sioux City and Baton Rouge) reported an aggregate
25.6% increase in casino revenues from $250.8&nbsp;million to $314.9&nbsp;million. In particular, Alton casino revenues increased from $84.7&nbsp;million to $112.1&nbsp;million. Riverside
casino revenues increased from $84.9&nbsp;million to $97.0&nbsp;million. Sioux City casino revenues increased from $28.0&nbsp;million to $34.8&nbsp;million, and Baton Rouge casino revenues
increased from $53.3&nbsp;million to $70.9&nbsp;million. Lawrenceburg casino revenues increased $35.7&nbsp;million, or 11.6% to $344.0&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000,
from $308.3&nbsp;million for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 1999. We experienced increases in both passengers and the average win per passenger for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000 versus the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999.
Additionally, the increase in revenues was partially attributable to favorable regulatory changes in Illinois, Missouri and Louisiana, as well as expanded capacity at Alton. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Casino
expenses increased 14.8% to $287.8&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000, from $250.6&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999. This
increase is primarily due to an increase of $23.1&nbsp;million in gaming taxes as a result of the overall increase in casino revenues. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Admissions</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Admissions revenues (net of complimentary admissions) were $6.1&nbsp;million for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2000, and $7.2&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999. Although the number of admissions increased in Lawrenceburg 1.0% in 2000 over 1999, net admission revenue
decreased as more customers were given complimentary admissions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Food, Beverage, and Other</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Food, beverage and other revenues increased from $58.0&nbsp;million to $66.1&nbsp;million for
the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000. This increase is primarily attributable to the overall increase in casino passengers for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000. Food, beverage and other
revenues, as a percent of casino revenues, has remained relatively steady at 10.0% in 2000 and 10.4% in 1999. Food, beverage and other net profit improved $3.0&nbsp;million to $19.5&nbsp;million
for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000. Increases in revenues and net profit came primarily from Alton and Lawrenceburg. Alton increased food and beverage revenues as it reopened one of its
restaurants, which was closed during the entire year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999. Lawrenceburg's increases were primarily due to a slight increase in admissions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During
2000, the Lawrenceburg Hotel generated $4.0&nbsp;million in net revenues and $1.5&nbsp;million of operating profit. The hotel occupancy percentage was 87.0% and the average
daily room rate, including promotional allowances, was $88. In 1999, the Lawrenceburg Hotel generated $4.2&nbsp;million in net revenues and $1.9&nbsp;million of operating profit. The hotel
occupancy percentage was 83.2% and the average daily room rate, including promotional allowances, was $84 during the months the hotel was open. The decrease in hotel net revenues and operating profit
reflects an increase in complimentary rooms to our customers. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Selling, General and Administrative</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Selling, general and administrative expenses increased 15.6% from $117.5 in 1999 to
$135.8&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000, due primarily to an increase at Lawrenceburg of $2.6&nbsp;million related to expanded marketing and $5.2&nbsp;million in
additional development payments to the city due to the increased gaming revenues. Marketing expenses increased $8.3&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000, remaining relatively
flat as a percent of casino revenues at approximately 7.0%. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Other Operating Expenses</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Other operating expenses increased from $27.9&nbsp;million in 1999 to $30.2&nbsp;million for
the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000 due primarily to increased vessel operating costs. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Depreciation and Amortization</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Depreciation and amortization increased slightly to $36.1&nbsp;million for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2000, from $34.1&nbsp;million in 1999. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>22</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=5,SEQ=23,EFW="2037759",CP="ARGOSY GAMING COMPANY",DN="1",CHK=476755,FOLIO='22',FILE='DISK011:[01CHI9.01CHI1459]DK1459B.;11',USER='MWEINST',CD='15-FEB-2001;11:28' -->
<A NAME="page_dk1459_1_23"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Interest Expense</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Net interest expense decreased $12.3&nbsp;million to $33.4&nbsp;million for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2000. The decrease in interest expense is attributable to the repayments on the credit facility in 2000, the refinancing completed during 1999 and the use of escrowed funds in
June&nbsp;2000 to redeem the untendered Mortgage Notes, both of which reduced our debt levels and a decrease of interest to a minority partner of $2.2&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Minority Interests&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Our minority interest expense increased by $5.5&nbsp;million to $40.5&nbsp;million for the year
ending December&nbsp;31, 2000. This increase is primarily attributable to improved operating results at Lawrenceburg. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Income Tax Expense&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>We recorded income tax expense of $31.2&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000
compared to income tax expense of $5.9&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999. Prior to 2000, our effective tax rate was impacted favorably due to the utilization of net operating
loss carryforwards. For the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999, income tax expense was offset by the reversal of a $10.0&nbsp;million valuation allowance related to prior federal income tax net
operating losses. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Net Income Before Extraordinary Item&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Net income before extraordinary items was $46.5&nbsp;million for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2000 compared to net income before extraordinary items of $36.4&nbsp;million in 1999 due primarily to the factors discussed above. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Extraordinary Loss&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>We recorded an extraordinary loss of $1.2&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000
related to completion of the final phase of the 1999 refinancing. This extraordinary loss is net of a $0.8&nbsp;million tax benefit. For the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999, we recorded an
extraordinary loss of $24.9&nbsp;million, net of a $13.5&nbsp;million tax benefit, related to the early extinguishment of debt in conjunction with the refinancing. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Net Income Attributable to Common Stockholders&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Net income attributable to common stockholders was $45.4&nbsp;million for
the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000 compared to $11.5&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999, due primarily to the factors discussed above. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="dk1459_year_ended_december_31,_1999_c__yea01893"> </A>
<A NAME="toc_dk1459_9"> </A>
<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999 compared to year ended December&nbsp;31, 1998    <BR>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Casino</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Casino revenues for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999, increased by 18.1% to
$559.1&nbsp;million from $473.5&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1998, due in part to a $44.0&nbsp;million increase in casino revenues at the Lawrenceburg casino, which
generated total casino revenues of $308.3&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999. Our other properties reported an aggregate 19.9% increase in casino revenues from $209.2 to
$250.8&nbsp;million. This improvement is primarily attributable to the regulatory changes in Illinois, Louisiana and Missouri and to the continued implementation of our operating and marketing
strategies. Specifically, Alton casino revenues increased from $67.8 to $84.7&nbsp;million due in part to dockside gaming effective June&nbsp;1999; Riverside casino revenues increased from $72.0
to $84.9&nbsp;million; Sioux City casino revenues increased from $22.6 to $28.0&nbsp;million and Baton Rouge casino revenues increased from $46.8 to $53.2&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Casino
expenses increased 13.0% to $250.6&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999, from $221.7&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1998. This
increase is primarily due to an increase of $17.9&nbsp;million in gaming taxes as a result of the overall increase in casino revenues. Baton Rouge casino expense is net of a $1.6&nbsp;million
decrease in admission taxes due to the elimination of an additional head tax, which commenced when construction began on the Baton Rouge hotel in July&nbsp;1999. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Admissions</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Admissions revenues (net of complimentary admissions) were $7.2&nbsp;million for the years ended
December&nbsp;31, 1999 and 1998. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Food, Beverage, and Other</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Food, beverage and other revenues increased from $51.1&nbsp;million to $58.0&nbsp;million for
the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999. This increase is attributable to the restaurants and the hotel at the Lawrenceburg property being open for the entire year in 1999. Food, beverage and other
net profit improved $6.0&nbsp;million to $16.5&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999. Alton, </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>23</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=6,SEQ=24,EFW="2037759",CP="ARGOSY GAMING COMPANY",DN="1",CHK=584448,FOLIO='23',FILE='DISK011:[01CHI9.01CHI1459]DK1459B.;11',USER='MWEINST',CD='15-FEB-2001;11:28' -->
<A NAME="page_dk1459_1_24"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
Riverside and Baton Rouge each reported relatively the same food and beverage revenues but decreases in food and beverage expenses. Alton's decrease was due to the closing of one of its restaurants
during the entire year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999 in conjunction with a major renovation.
Riverside's and Baton Rouge's decreases were primarily due to the decreased use of food and beverage as promotional items. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Lawrenceburg hotel contributed $4.2&nbsp;million in net revenues and $1.9&nbsp;million of operating profit. The hotel occupancy percentage was 83.2% and the average daily room
rate, including promotional allowances, was $84. In 1998, the hotel occupancy percentage was 73.5% and the average daily room rate, including promotional allowances, was $79 during the months the
hotel was open. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Selling, General and Administrative</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Selling, general and administrative expenses increased 21.7% to $117.5&nbsp;million
for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999, due primarily to an increase at Lawrenceburg of $3.9&nbsp;million related to expanded marketing and $4.5&nbsp;million in additional development
payments to the city due to the increased gaming revenues. Corporate expenses increased due to expenses of $1.8&nbsp;million related to a severance and settlement arrangement and $3.1&nbsp;million
related to incentive compensation. Marketing expenses increased $4.8&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999 but remained relatively flat, at approximately 7%, as a percentage of
casino revenues. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Other Operating Expenses</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Other operating expenses increased from $26.6&nbsp;million in 1998 to $27.9&nbsp;million for
the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Depreciation and Amortization</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Depreciation and amortization increased slightly to $34.1&nbsp;million for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 1999, from $33.4&nbsp;million in 1998. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Interest Expense</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Net interest expense decreased $8.2&nbsp;million to $45.7&nbsp;million for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 1999. The decrease in interest expense is primarily attributable to the refinancing completed during 1999 and a decrease of interest to a minority partner of $3.0&nbsp;million.
This decrease, however, was offset by a decrease in capitalized interest of $1.0&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Minority Interests&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Our minority interest expense increased by $8.8&nbsp;million to $35.0&nbsp;million for the year
ending December&nbsp;31, 1999. This increase is primarily attributable to improved income at our Indiana Partnership. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Income Tax Expense&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>We recorded income tax expense of $5.9&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999
compared to income tax expense of $1.1&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1998. Our effective tax rate has been impacted favorably in 1999 and 1998 due to the utilization of net
operating
loss carryforwards. Income tax expense was offset by the reversal of a $10.0&nbsp;million valuation allowance related to prior federal income tax net operating losses that are expected to be
utilized in 2000. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Net Income Before Extraordinary Item&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Net income before extraordinary items increased to $36.4&nbsp;million for the year
ended December&nbsp;31, 1999 from $6.6&nbsp;million in 1998 due primarily to the factors discussed above. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Extraordinary Loss&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>We recorded an extraordinary loss of $24.9&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999
related to the early extinguishment of debt in conjunction with a refinancing. This extraordinary loss is net of a $13.5&nbsp;million tax benefit. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Net Income Attributable to Common Stockholders&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Net income attributable to common stockholders was $11.5&nbsp;million for
the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999 compared to $5.7&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1998, due primarily to the factors discussed above. </FONT></P>

<A NAME="page_dk1459_1_25"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="dk1459_liquidity_and_capital_resources"> </A>
<A NAME="toc_dk1459_10"> </A>
<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Liquidity and Capital Resources    <BR>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During 2000, we generated cash flows from operating activities of $158.2&nbsp;million compared to $126.7&nbsp;million for 1999. This increase is
attributable to the improved operations at each of our five casino locations. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During
2000, we used cash flows for investing activities of $44.0&nbsp;million versus $37.1&nbsp;million for 1999. Capital expenditures in 2000 consisted of $13.6&nbsp;million
in maintenance capital, primarily related to slot machine replacements and $19.6&nbsp;million for expansion projects, including construction of a 300 room hotel in Baton Rouge. During 2000,
$9.2&nbsp;million in cash flows were used to purchase the minority interest in the Sioux City partnership. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During
2000, we used $101.5&nbsp;million in cash flows for financing activities compared to $132.3&nbsp;million in cash flows for the same period in 1999. During 2000,
$56.4&nbsp;million in cash flows were used to make repayments on the line of credit. Cash flows in both 2000 and 1999 were used to repay loans related to our Lawrenceburg casino, partner equity
distributions related to the Lawrenceburg partnership and for payments on installment contracts and other long term debt. In 1999, we received proceeds of
$200&nbsp;million from the issuance of subordinated notes and $161.8&nbsp;million from a bank credit facility. During 1999, we also repaid long-term debt of $327.7&nbsp;million,
placed $25.2&nbsp;million in funds in an escrow to retire the First Mortgage Notes, repaid $58.0&nbsp;million on the credit facility, used $30.6&nbsp;million to pay premiums to retire existing
debt in connection with our refinancing and used $8.7&nbsp;million to pay fees in connection with the refinancing. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;At
December&nbsp;31, 2000, we had approximately $59.4&nbsp;million of cash and cash equivalents, including approximately $38.8&nbsp;million held at the Indiana Partnership.
During June&nbsp;2000, we redeemed the remaining $22.2&nbsp;million of First Mortgage Notes that were not tendered in the June&nbsp;1999 refinancing. At December&nbsp;31, 2000, we had
outstanding $200&nbsp;million of Senior Subordinated Notes, which were issued in June&nbsp;1999 and are due in June&nbsp;2009 and $47.4&nbsp;million on a senior secured revolving credit
facility. As of February&nbsp;13, 2001 availability under the credit facility was approximately $146&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We
have made a significant investment in property and equipment and plan to make significant additional investments at our existing properties. In 2001, we expect maintenance capital
expenditures primarily related to the purchase of new gaming product and facility enhancements to be approximately $19.1&nbsp;million and final expenditures related to the Baton Rouge hotel to be
approximately $7.3&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Both
of our partners in the Indiana partnership have exercised their put rights under the terms of the Lawrenceburg partnership agreement. In December&nbsp;2000, we reached an
agreement with Conseco to purchase its 29% limited partner interest for $260&nbsp;million, including the repayment of Conseco's preferred equity interest and outstanding partner loans and to settle
all pending litigation between us and Conseco. In January&nbsp;2001, we reached an agreement with Centaur to purchase its 13.5% limited partnership interest for $105&nbsp;million. We anticipate
closing the purchase of the Lawrenceburg casino limited partner interests in one or two separate transactions in the first quarter of 2001 subject to, and promptly following, receipt of all necessary
regulatory approvals. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We
have also agreed to provide up to $40&nbsp;million as part of our agreement to develop and operate a proposed casino in Kenosha, Wisconsin. The proposed casino would be owned by
the Menominee Indian Tribe of Wisconsin. Of this $40&nbsp;million commitment, we have advanced $1&nbsp;million during 2001 and will advance up to an additional $4&nbsp;million upon the tribe
receiving approval from the United States Bureau of Indian Affairs to place the proposed casino property in federal trust. We also have committed to provide a $30&nbsp;million subordinated note
concurrent with, and conditioned upon, the tribe's institutional debt offering that is anticipated to finance the project. In addition, we will provide a $5&nbsp;million completion guarantee on the
construction of the proposed facility. This project and our funding commitment are subject to numerous regulatory approvals. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;To
provide funding for our purchase of Conseco's and Centaur's limited partnership interests and our Kenosha casino development commitment, we are in the process of amending and
restating our </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>25</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=8,SEQ=26,EFW="2037759",CP="ARGOSY GAMING COMPANY",DN="1",CHK=667315,FOLIO='25',FILE='DISK011:[01CHI9.01CHI1459]DK1459B.;11',USER='MWEINST',CD='15-FEB-2001;11:28' -->
<A NAME="page_dk1459_1_26"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
existing credit facility to, among other things, increase borrowing availability to $400&nbsp;million. We believe that cash on hand, operating cash flows, available capacity under our amended and
restated credit facility and the net proceeds from our recent $150&nbsp;million Senior Subordinated Notes offering, will be sufficient to fund the purchase of Conseco's and Centaur's limited
partnership interests, our commitment to develop the Kenosha casino and our current operating, capital expenditure and debt service obligations. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="dk1459_market_risk_#151;interest_rate_sensitivity"> </A>
<A NAME="toc_dk1459_11"> </A>
<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Market Risk&#151;Interest Rate Sensitivity    <BR>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The market risk inherent in our financial instruments is the potential loss in fair value arising from adverse changes in interest rates. Currently, we do not
use interest rate derivative instruments to manage exposure to interest rate changes as the majority of our indebtedness is financed at fixed rates. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
following table provides information about our debt obligations that are sensitive to changes in interest rates. The following table presents principal cash flows and related
weighted-average interest rates by expected maturity dates and estimated fair value of our debt obligations. </FONT></P>

<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>ARGOSY GAMING COMPANY<BR>  NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS<BR>  (In thousands except share and per share data)    <BR>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>1. Summary of Significant Accounting Policies  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Basis of Presentation&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Argosy Gaming Company (collectively with its subsidiaries, "Argosy" or
"Company") is engaged in the business of providing casino style gaming and related entertainment to the public and, through its subsidiaries or joint ventures, operates riverboat casinos in Alton,
Illinois; Lawrenceburg, Indiana; Riverside, Missouri; Baton Rouge, Louisiana; and Sioux City, Iowa. Indiana Gaming Company, L.P. ("Indiana Partnership"), a limited partnership in which the Company is
general partner and holds a 57.5% partnership interest, operates a casino and hotel in Lawrenceburg, Indiana. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
preparation of financial statements in conformity with generally accepted accounting principles requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the amounts
reported in the financial statements and accompanying notes. Actual results could differ from those estimates. The consolidated financial statements include the accounts of Argosy and its controlled
subsidiaries and partnerships. All significant intercompany transactions have been eliminated.&nbsp;&nbsp;Under certain conditions, subsidiaries are required to obtain approval from state
gaming authorities before making distributions to Argosy. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Certain
1999 and 1998 amounts have been reclassified to conform to the 2000 presentation. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Cash and Cash Equivalents&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>The Company considers cash and all highly liquid investments with an original maturity of three
months or less to be cash equivalents. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Property and Equipment&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Property and equipment are recorded at cost. Leasehold improvements are amortized over the life of
the respective lease. Depreciation is computed on the straight-line method over the following estimated useful lives: </FONT></P>

<!-- User-specified TAGGED TABLE -->
<DIV ALIGN="CENTER"><TABLE WIDTH="80%" BORDER=0 CELLSPACING=0 CELLPADDING=0>

<TD WIDTH="3%"><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="20%" ALIGN="RIGHT"><FONT SIZE=2>5 to 33 years</FONT></TD>
</TR>
<TR BGCOLOR="White" VALIGN="TOP">
<TD WIDTH="77%"><FONT SIZE=2>Riverboats, docks and improvements</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%"><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="20%" ALIGN="RIGHT"><FONT SIZE=2>5 to 20 years</FONT></TD>
</TR>

</TR>

<!-- end of user-specified TAGGED TABLE -->


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Impairment of Long-Lived Assets&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>When events or circumstances indicate that the carrying amount of
long-lived assets to be held and used might not be recoverable, the expected future undiscounted cash flows from the assets is estimated and compared with the carrying amount of the
assets. If the sum of the estimated undiscounted cash flows is less than the carrying amount of the assets, an impairment loss is recorded. The impairment loss is measured by comparing the fair value
of the assets with their carrying amount. Long-lived assets that are held for disposal are reported at the lower of the assets' carrying amount or fair value less costs related to the
assets' disposition. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Deferred Finance Costs&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Deferred finance costs are amortized over the life of the respective loans using the effective
interest method. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Goodwill and Other Intangible Assets&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Goodwill represents the cost in excess of fair value of net assets acquired, and is
amortized over lives up to 40&nbsp;years. Other intangible assets, primarily payments to cities, are amortized over the lives of the respective leases or development agreements including extensions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Revenues and Promotional Allowances&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>The Company recognizes as casino revenues the net win from gaming activities, which is
the difference between gaming wins and losses. Admissions, hotel and other revenue is recognized at the time the related service is performed. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
retail value of admissions, hotel rooms, food, beverage and other items which were provided to customers without charge has been included in revenues, and a corresponding amount
has been </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>33</FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On
June&nbsp;8, 1999, the Company issued $200,000 of Senior Subordinated Notes due 2009 ("Subordinated Notes") and entered into a five year $200,000 Senior Secured revolving bank
credit agreement ("Credit Facility"). The Credit Facility is secured by liens on substantially all of the Company's assets, and the Company's subsidiaries are co-borrowers. The Company's
joint-venture subsidiary that operates the Argosy Casino&nbsp;&amp; Hotel in Lawrenceburg is not a co-borrower nor are the assets of the subsidiary pledged in either agreement. All of the
Company's wholly-owned operating subsidiaries guarantee the Subordinated Notes. The Company's joint-venture subsidiary that operates the Argosy Casino&nbsp;&amp; Hotel in Lawrenceburg is not a guarantor
of the Subordinated Notes. The Subordinated Notes rank junior to
all of the senior indebtedness of the Company, including borrowings under the Credit Facility and the subsidiary guarantees of the Subordinated Notes rank junior to the senior indebtedness of the
subsidiary guarantors. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Subordinated Notes and the Credit Facility contain certain restrictions on the payment of dividends on the Company's common stock and the occurrence of additional indebtedness, as
well as other typical debt covenants. In addition, the Credit Facility requires the Company to maintain certain financial ratios. The Credit Facility provides for, within two years, additional
borrowing availability of $75,000 to be used for general corporate purposes and a further $150,000 increase to fund the purchase of all outstanding minority interests in the Lawrenceburg partnership.
The increases in the Credit Facility are subject to a number of contingencies including lender approval. The Credit Facility is subject to scheduled reductions of 2.5% to 5.0% per quarter, beginning
September&nbsp;2000, of the total borrowing availability. The Company has a $1.9&nbsp;million letter of credit outstanding at December&nbsp;31, 2000. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
1999, the Company used the net proceeds from the issuance of the Subordinated Notes, $25,000 in borrowings under the Credit Facility and approximately $51,000 of cash on hand to
tender for and retire approximately $213,000 of its $235,000 outstanding 13<SUP>1</SUP>/<SMALL>4</SMALL>% First Mortgage Notes due 2004 ("Mortgage Notes"). Under terms of the Credit Facility, the Company was
required to redeem the remaining $22,242 of untendered Mortgage Notes on June&nbsp;1, 2000 and placed monies in escrow to fund </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>35</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=3,SEQ=36,EFW="2037759",CP="ARGOSY GAMING COMPANY",DN="1",CHK=848215,FOLIO='35',FILE='DISK011:[01CHI9.01CHI1459]DO1459A.;12',USER='SLYUBOM',CD='15-FEB-2001;15:38' -->
<A NAME="page_do1459_1_36"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
the remaining principal, interest payments and the June&nbsp;2000 redemption premium. At December&nbsp;31, 1999, the remaining escrow balance of $25,244 was classified as restricted cash in
escrow. During June&nbsp;2000, the Company used the escrowed funds to redeem the untendered Mortgage Notes and recorded an extraordinary loss of $1,154, net of a tax benefit of $770. On
July&nbsp;7, 1999, the Company redeemed all of its outstanding 12% Convertible Subordinated Notes due 2001 ("Convertible Notes"). During 1999, the Company used borrowings of $105,000 under the
Credit Facility and approximately $13,700 of cash to redeem the Convertible Notes. In connection with the early extinguishment of the Mortgage Notes and Convertible Notes during 1999, the Company
recorded an extraordinary loss of $24,920 net of a tax benefit of $13,500. </FONT></P>

expense for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2000, 1999 and 1998, was $34,768 (net of $717 capitalized), $48,594 (net of $115 capitalized) and $57,487 (net of $1,086
capitalized), respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>6. Convertible Preferred Stock and Warrants  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On June&nbsp;16, 1998, the Company issued $8,000 of Series&nbsp;A Convertible Preferred Stock ("Preferred Shares"), together with warrants to purchase an
additional 292,612 shares of Common Stock at $3.89 per share. The warrants expire in 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Preferred Shares provided for a 4% dividend per annum, payable in cash and/or in kind, at the time of conversion or maturity, at the Company's option. Through December&nbsp;31,
1998, the Preferred Shares had been converted into 1,331,980 shares of common stock. During the year ended December&nbsp;31, 1999, the remaining Preferred Shares were converted into 2,310,011 shares
of common stock. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This
transaction provided for put and call options which, subject to certain restrictions and limitations, allowed for up to an additional $8,000 of Preferred Shares and Warrants to
be issued. In December&nbsp;1998, the Company amended its agreement with the holders of the Preferred Shares to terminate both the holders' right to purchase, and the Company's right to require such
holders to
purchase, the additional $8,000 tranche of Preferred Shares and related warrants. The Company paid $625 to amend the agreement, and this amount is included in preferred stock dividends and accretion
in the accompanying statement of income for 1998. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During
1999, 201,172 warrants were converted into 172,496 shares of common stock. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
valuation allowance relates to state deferred tax assets established under SFAS&nbsp;109 for Louisiana net operating loss carryforwards of approximately $30,000 and $38,600 at
December&nbsp;31, 2000 and 1999, respectively. These loss carryforwards, which will expire from 2012 through 2019, will be carried forward to future years for possible utilization. During 1999, the
Company recognized a $10,000 tax benefit representing prior federal income tax net operating losses. </FONT></P>

Company issued 69,319, 2,494,793 and 1,331,980 shares of additional common stock resulting from the conversion of Preferred Stock, the exercise of stock options, conversion of
debentures and the conversion of warrants during 2000, 1999 and 1998, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>11. Stock Option Plans  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company adopted the Argosy Gaming Company Stock Option Plan, as amended, ("Stock Option Plan"), which provides for the grant of non-qualified
stock options for up to 2,500,000 shares of common stock to key employees of the Company. These options expire 10&nbsp;years after their respective grant dates and become exercisable over a
specified vesting period. At December&nbsp;31, 2000, options for 706,191 shares are exercisable under the Stock Option Plan at a weighted average price of $3.87. The weighted average contractual
life of outstanding options at December&nbsp;31, 2000 is approximately 7.2&nbsp;years and the weighted average exercise price of options outstanding is $5.91. The weighted average fair value of
options granted was $9.90, $3.07 and $1.40, during 2000, 1999 and 1998, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On
November&nbsp;7, 1997 ("Grant Date"), the Company's board of directors approved a plan that allowed certain employees to exchange their existing stock options for an amount of
options equal to the number of options to be exchanged multiplied by a fraction: the numerator of which is $4.25 (closing price on Grant Date) and the denominator of which is the prior option price.
This exchange of options was finalized during 1998, and options for 625,373 shares of stock were exchanged for options for 157,524 shares of stock. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Company also has adopted the Argosy Gaming Company 1993 Directors Stock Option Plan ("Directors Option Plan"), which provides for a total of 50,000 shares of common stock to be
authorized and reserved for issuance. The Directors Option Plan provides for the grant of non-qualified stock options at fair market value to non-employee directors of the
Company as of the date such individuals become directors of the Company. These options expire five years after their respective grant dates and become exercisable over a specified vesting period. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>39</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=3,SEQ=40,EFW="2037759",CP="ARGOSY GAMING COMPANY",DN="1",CHK=93710,FOLIO='39',FILE='DISK011:[01CHI9.01CHI1459]DQ1459A.;11',USER='ABLIJDE',CD='15-FEB-2001;15:33' -->
<A NAME="page_dq1459_1_40"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company follows Accounting Principles Board Opinion No.&nbsp;25, "Accounting for Stock Issued to Employees" ("APB 25"), and related interpretations in accounting for its
employee stock options. Under APB 25, the Company does not recognize compensation expense when the exercise price of employee stock options equals or exceeds the market price of the underlying stock
on the date of grant. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Company has adopted the disclosure only provisions of Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;123 ("SFAS&nbsp;123"), "Accounting for Stock Based Compensation."
Accordingly, no compensation expense has been recognized for either stock plan. Had the valuation methods under SFAS&nbsp;123 been used for the Company's stock option grants, the fiscal 2000 pro
forma net income attributable to common stockholders would have been $45,007 and the pro forma diluted income per share would have been $1.54. The fair value of each option was estimated on the date
of grant using the Black-Scholes option pricing model with the following assumptions: dividend yield of zero; expected volatility 57%; risk-free interest rate of 6%; and expected option
life of five years. The fiscal 1999 pro forma net income attributable to common stockholders would have been $11,089 and the pro forma diluted income per share would have been $0.38. The fair value of
each option was estimated on the date of grant using the Black-Scholes option pricing model with the following assumptions: dividend yield of zero; expected volatility 56.5%; risk-free
interest rate of 6%, and expected option life of three years. The fiscal 1998 pro forma net income attributable to common stockholders would have been $5,579 and the pro forma diluted income per share
would have been $0.23. The fair value of each option was estimated on the date of grant using the Black-Scholes option pricing model with the following assumptions: dividend yield of zero; expected
volatility 52.7%; risk-free interest rate of 6% and expected option life of three years. These pro forma amounts may not be representative of future disclosures because the estimated fair
value of the options is amortized to expense over the vesting period and additional options may be granted in the future. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="page_ds1459_1_41"> </A> </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><B>12. Restricted Stock  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company issued 165,000 shares of restricted common stock to certain new employees in 1997. The value of these shares at their respective grant dates ranged
from $3.13 to $3.63. In 1998, 66,000 shares of the restricted stock vested, and in 2000, 99,000 shares vested. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Compensation
expense was amortized over the period from the date of grant until the respective vesting dates. Compensation expense of $39, $113 and $239 was recognized in 2000, 1999
and 1998, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>13. Employees Benefit Plan  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company established a 401(k) defined-contribution plan, which covers substantially all of its full-time employees. Participants can contribute
a portion of their eligible salaries (as defined) subject to maximum limits, as determined by provisions of the Internal Revenue Code. The Company will match a portion of participants' contributions
in an amount determined annually by the Company. Expense recognized under the Plan was approximately $1,715, $1,145 and $1,134 in 2000, 1999 and 1998, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>14. Subsidiary Guarantors  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Credit Facility is secured by a first lien on substantially all of the Company's assets and the Company's subsidiaries are co-borrowers. The Company's
joint-venture subsidiary that operates the Argosy Casino Lawrenceburg is not a co-borrower nor are the assets of the subsidiary pledged. The Subordinated Notes are fully and unconditionally
guaranteed, on a joint and several basis, by the following wholly-owned subsidiaries of the Company: Alton Gaming Company, The Missouri Gaming Company, The St. Louis Gaming Company, Iowa Gaming
Company, Argosy of Iowa, Inc., Jazz Enterprises, Inc., Argosy of Louisiana, Inc., Catfish Queen Partnership in Commendam, Centroplex Centre Convention Hotel LLC and The Indiana Gaming Company (the
"Guarantors"). The Company's joint-venture subsidiary that operates the Argosy Casino &amp; Hotel in Lawrenceburg is not a guarantor of the Subordinated Notes. The Subordinated Notes rank junior to all of
the senior indebtedness of the Company, including borrowings under the Credit Facility. </FONT></P>

<DT><FONT SIZE=2>(1)</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>The
second quarter of 2000 includes a $6,800 pre-tax charge related to the write-off of the former landing facility at our Alton property.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT><FONT SIZE=2>(2)</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>The
second quarter of 2000 includes an extraordinary loss of $1,200 related to completion of the final phase of the 1999 refinancing.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT><FONT SIZE=2>(3)</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>The
second and third quarters of 1999 include extraordinary losses related to the refinancing and were $34.8&nbsp;million and $3,600, respectively. The fourth quarter of 1999
extraordinary item represents a $13,500 tax benefit related to the refinancing which was recognized with the reversal of deferred tax valuation reserves and the resulting tax provision. </FONT></DD></DL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>17. Commitments and Contingent Liabilities  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Lawrenceburg, Indiana&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>In December&nbsp;2000 and January&nbsp;2001, we reached agreements with
our minority partners in the Lawrenceburg casino to purchase their combined 42.5% limited partnership interests for $365,000, including the repayment of Conseco's preferred equity interest and
outstanding partner loans. In connection with the December agreement, we agreed to settle all pending litigation between
Conseco and us upon purchase of their minority interest. Under our settlement agreement with Conseco, the Company is required to purchase their 29% minority interest no later than March&nbsp;1,
2001. </FONT></P>

<A NAME="page_ds1459_1_51"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The purchase of these minority interests is subject to, and will be consummated in one or two separate transactions promptly following receipt of all necessary regulatory approvals
and satisfaction of all customary closing conditions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Company has agreed to provide up to $40,000 as part of our agreement to develop and operate a proposed casino in Kenosha, Wisconsin. The proposed casino would be owned by the
Menominee Indian Tribe of Wisconsin. Of this $40,000 commitment, we have advanced $1,000 during 2001 and will advance up to an additional $4,000 upon the tribe receiving approval from the United
States Bureau of Indian Affairs to place the proposed casino property in federal trust. We also have committed to provide a $30,000 subordinated note concurrent with, and conditioned upon, the tribe's
institutional debt offering that is anticipated to finance the project. In addition, we will provide a $5,000 completion guarantee on the construction of the proposed facility. This project and our
funding commitment are subject to numerous regulatory approvals. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Company is subject, from time to time, to various legal and regulatory proceedings, in the ordinary course of business. The Company believes that current proceedings will not have
a material effect on the financial condition of the Company or the results of its operations. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>18. Subsequent Event  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On February&nbsp;8, 2001, the Company raised $159,000 through the issuance of $150,000 of additional 10<SUP>3</SUP>/<SMALL>4</SMALL>% Senior Subordinated Notes due 2009
at a price of 106% of par. The proceeds, together with borrowings under our credit facility, will be used to acquire Conseco's 29.0% minority interest in our Lawrenceburg partnership for $260,000 and
to repay outstanding indebtedness. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Board of Directors<BR>
Argosy Gaming Company </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We
have audited the accompanying consolidated balance sheets of Argosy Gaming Company as of December&nbsp;31, 2000 and 1999 and the related consolidated statements of income,
stockholders' equity and cash flows for each of the three years in the period ended December&nbsp;31, 2000. These financial statements are the responsibility of the Company's management. Our
responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial statements based on our audits. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We
conducted our audits in accordance with auditing standards generally accepted in the United States. Those standards require that we plan and perform the audit to obtain reasonable
assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement. An audit includes examining, on a test basis, evidence supporting the amounts and disclosures in the financial
statements. An audit also includes assessing the accounting principles used and significant estimates made by management, as well as evaluating the overall financial statement presentation. We believe
that our audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinion. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
our opinion, the financial statements referred to above present fairly, in all material respects, the consolidated financial position of Argosy Gaming Company at
December&nbsp;31, 2000 and 1999 and the consolidated results of its operations and its cash flows for each of the three years in the period ended December&nbsp;31, 2000 in conformity with
accounting principles generally accepted in the United States. </FONT></P>

                         ARTICLES OF INCORPORATION

                                   OF

                         DES MOINES GAMING COMPANY


To the Secretary of State
    State of Iowa:


      Pursuant to Section 202 of the Iowa Business Corporation Act, the
undersigned, acting as incorporator of a corporation, adopts the following
articles of incorporation for the corporation.

1.   The name of the corporation is: Des Moines Gaming Company.

2.   The number of shares the corporation is authorized to issue is: 1000
     shares of common stock, without par value.

3.   The street address of the initial registered office of the corporation
     is: c/o CT Corporation System, 2222 Grand Avenue, Des Moines, Iowa 50312
     and the initial registered agent of the corporation at such address is:
     CT Corporation System.

4.   The name and address of the sole incorporator is:

     Seka Jajic Kaplarevic                  35 W. Wacker Dr., Chicago, IL 60601

5.   The corporation shall indemnify and advance expenses for the benefit of
     any officer, director, employee or agent of the corporation when a bona
     fide claim is made against such officer, director, employee or agent
     when such claim arises out of the ordinary acts and doings of
     such officer, director, employee or agent in the ordinary course of
     business. This indemnification will be pursuant to Sections 490.832 and
     490.856 of the 1989 Code of Iowa, as amended. This indemnification shall
     be controlled by these statutes as amended from time to time.

IN WITNESS WHEREOF, the undersigned has executed these articles of
incorporation this 5th day of October, 1994.


                                              By:  /s/ Seka J. Kaplarevic
                                                  ----------------------------
                                              Seka Jajic Kaplarevic
                                              Sole Incorporator

                                       [STAMP]
<PAGE>

                                   OF

                         DES MOINES GAMING COMPANY



TO THE SECRETARY OF STATE OF THE STATE OF IOWA:


      Pursuant to Section 1002 or 1006 of the Iowa Business Corporation Act,
the undersigned corporation adopts the following amendment to the
corporation's articles of incorporation.

      1.   The name of the corporation is Des Moines Gaming Company.

      2.   The corporation's name is being changed to Argosy of Iowa, Inc.

      3.   The date of adoption of the amendment was February 15, 1995.


      The amendment was adopted by the board of directors without action by
the shareholders pursuant to Section 490.1002 of the Iowa Business
Corporation Act.


                                           Des Moines Gaming Company

                                             /s/ J. Thomas Long
                                          ----------------------------
                                           Name: J. THOMAS LONG
                                           Title: CEO

                                       [STAMP]
